         <div class="section-content">
          <div class="section-inner sectionLayout--insetColumn">
           <h1 name="1882" id="1882" class="graf graf--h3 graf--leading graf--title">The 100% correct way to validate email addresses</h1>
           <p name="cf51" id="cf51" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">Congratulations. From this day forward, you will no longer squander your time trying to work out the perfect regex to validate email addresses. You will also never again run the risk of rejecting what is, in fact, a strange, valid email address.</p>
           <p name="5440" id="5440" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">The trick is to first define what we mean by ‘valid’.</p>
           <p name="23fa" id="23fa" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">We are developers, we are technical folk, so it’s no surprise that the prevailing wisdom is to check that it <a href="http://www.ex-parrot.com/pdw/Mail-RFC822-Address.html" data-href="http://www.ex-parrot.com/pdw/Mail-RFC822-Address.html" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">matches</a> the official criteria, some examples of the diversity of the official criteria are…</p>
           <figure name="be69" id="be69" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 637px; max-height: 483px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 75.8%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*dPw1Aj7sWsp9ledwBuvIHw.png" data-width="637" data-height="483">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*dPw1Aj7sWsp9ledwBuvIHw.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*dPw1Aj7sWsp9ledwBuvIHw.png">
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*dPw1Aj7sWsp9ledwBuvIHw.png">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
            <figcaption class="imageCaption">
             <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Email_address#Valid_email_addresses" data-href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Email_address#Valid_email_addresses" class="markup--anchor markup--figure-anchor" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Email_address#Valid_email_addresses</a>
            </figcaption>
           </figure>
           <p name="d9d2" id="d9d2" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">But I say pish! to prevailing wisdom, so…</p>
           <h3 name="17cc" id="17cc" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--p">Everything you know is&nbsp;wrong</h3>
           <p name="99a5" id="99a5" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">Instead of the above approach that largely ignores reality, I believe there are two questions we need to ask:</p>
           <ol class="postList">
            <li name="bf1b" id="bf1b" class="graf graf--li graf-after--p">Did the user understand that they were supposed to type an email address into this field?</li>
            <li name="c2c2" id="c2c2" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li">Did the user correctly type their email address into this field?</li>
           </ol>
           <p name="7946" id="7946" class="graf graf--p graf-after--li">If you have a well laid-out form with a label that says “email”, and the user enters an ‘@’ symbol somewhere, then it’s safe to say they understood that they were supposed to be entering an email address. Easy.</p>
           <p name="3a65" id="3a65" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Next, we want to do some validation to ascertain if they correctly entered <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">their</em> email address.</p>
           <p name="56e8" id="56e8" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Not possible.</p>
           <p name="f98a" id="f98a" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">It’s important that you agree with me on this point: <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">it’s not possible</em>.</p>
           <p name="9e46" id="9e46" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">I know what you’re thinking. “But it <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">helps, </em>right?” That’s like saying that opening and closing your fridge really quickly conserves energy and helps fight climate change. Sure, it helps, if we want to be slaves to the word ‘help’. But most people would agree you have a promising career in a straight jacket if you’re unnecessarily rattling your pickle jars for the benefit of the polar bears.</p>
           <h3 name="22b8" id="22b8" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--p">Let’s explore</h3>
           <p name="2546" id="2546" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">Let’s imagine that my email address is <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">davidgilbertson@example.com</strong>. That’s 27 stabs at the keyboard that could go awry. Any mistype will <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">definitely </em>result in an <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">incorrect </strong>email address but only <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">maybe</em> result in an <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">invalid </strong>email address.</p>
           <p name="c416" id="c416" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">[epiphany]</p>
           <p name="99c5" id="99c5" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Even if the sun shone through my window and I was visited by a particularly savage sneeze (I suffer from Autosomal Dominant Compelling Helio-Ophthalmic Outburst Syndrome*) and I typed out <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">#!$%&amp;’*+-/=?^_`{}|~</strong><a href="http://twitter.com/example" data-href="http://twitter.com/example" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" title="Twitter profile for @example" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">@example</strong></a><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">.com</strong> by mistake, I would still pass the most thorough email ‘validation’ techniques. (The flip side is I fail and be told my address isn’t valid when it is! On a whim I just emailed the person at <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">#!$%&amp;’*+-/=?^_`{}|~</strong><a href="http://twitter.com/example" data-href="http://twitter.com/example" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" title="Twitter profile for @example" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">@example</strong></a><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">.com </strong>and she said she gets super pissed off when told that her email address isn’t valid. She regrets buying the example.com domain, too, but won’t give it up, just like the guy that’s got milk.com. We got chatting and it turns out she only lives a few blocks from me and also collects vintage cameras; we’re playing golf next week. I think maybe she’s the one. I should probably close these brackets and get on with the story.)</p>
           <p name="8e26" id="8e26" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">So what are the odds that any one typo would result in an invalid email address? We will build a statistical model! Let’s look at, say, the ‘g’. I am more likely to mis-type with a letter on the visible keyboard with no shift key required (I apply a weighting to non-modified keys in the model). From all of the tappable keys on a physical keyboard, there are six characters that, while not completely invalid, are only valid in certain cases: <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">[]\;,</strong> and <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">space</strong>. 6 out of 48. A 12% chance.</p>
           <p name="7529" id="7529" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">But an off-by-one error is more likely. For example hitting the neighbouring ‘h’ key instead of ‘g’. So from a list of 117 million email addresses I have calculated the frequency of occurrence of each character and for each, noted which keys lie closest on the keyboard, and factored in the likelihood that a mis-stroke will create an invalid email address. (I know hacking LinkedIn just to make a point about email validation is a bit extreme, but it is important to back up one’s opinions with data).</p>
           <p name="0656" id="0656" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">For example, ‘e’ is considered a low risk of invalidating, because all surrounding keys would still result in a valid email address. But ‘p’ has <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">[</strong> and&nbsp;<strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">;</strong> within striking distance! So although it’s less common than ‘e’, it carries a higher risk of resulting in an invalid email address if missed.</p>
           <p name="981a" id="981a" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">I also consider the relative dexterity of the fingers. We all know that the pinky is the retarded cousin of the finger family, so that is factored in as well.</p>
          </div>
          <div class="section-inner sectionLayout--outsetColumn">
           <figure name="18ce" id="18ce" class="graf graf--figure graf--layoutOutsetCenter graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 1000px; max-height: 349px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 34.9%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*qkkv0iT-g7cMAN3XjpOEow.png" data-width="1123" data-height="392" data-action="zoom" data-action-value="1*qkkv0iT-g7cMAN3XjpOEow.png">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*qkkv0iT-g7cMAN3XjpOEow.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/2000/1*qkkv0iT-g7cMAN3XjpOEow.png">
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/2000/1*qkkv0iT-g7cMAN3XjpOEow.png">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
            <figcaption class="imageCaption">
             A graphical representation of the model showing the strike zone around the P, accounting for the shortcomings of the&nbsp;pinky.
            </figcaption>
           </figure>
          </div>
          <div class="section-inner sectionLayout--insetColumn">
           <p name="1c79" id="1c79" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">Now, let’s say Silkie (fox) sits on the shift key <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">and </em>I hit the wrong key on the keyboard. I’m in danger of getting one of 6 bad keys: <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">@:”&lt;&gt; </strong>and <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">space</strong>. And again, those bad keys are only invalid in certain circumstances. And since it’s more likely that the shift key would be down only for the letters on either side of the @ symbol, and ‘l’ on either side of the @ is considered particularly dangerous.</p>
           <p name="7278" id="7278" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">The above is all for a single key, but if I mistype a second key, it is possible that I turn an invalid email address back into a valid one (e.g. adding a \ next to a \). This is, of course, factored into the model.</p>
           <p name="584d" id="584d" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">It goes without saying that I’ve gone to a similar level of effort to account for soft keyboards.</p>
           <p name="23f2" id="23f2" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Remember too that if I mistype the @ symbol, the error will be caught by step one above where I actually check for the existence of an @ as a proxy for a user’s <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">intent</em> to enter an email address.</p>
           <p name="a821" id="a821" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">I also built in some general common sense: people with aol email addresses are sloppy typers. Daryls tend to poke at the keys with only their index fingers like they’re afraid each key will burn them. People with ‘z’ in their name use mechanical keyboards and rarely make mistakes. Your basic human axioms.</p>
           <p name="db0e" id="db0e" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">I also factored in the fact that any dot before the @ in gmail addresses is ignored and that ‘f’ and ‘h’ are pretty much the same letter when you think about it.</p>
           <h3 name="f913" id="f913" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--p">The result</h3>
           <p name="99e1" id="99e1" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">So with all of that taken into account, I ran the 117 million email addresses through the model. And the odds that an incorrect email address will be caught by email validation is&nbsp;…</p>
           <p name="0c58" id="0c58" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">0.00000000000000000000000000000000000000625%</p>
           <p name="76ac" id="76ac" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">I’m afraid I don’t have time to type out the algorithm that totally exists and is indisputably perfect, so you’ll have to take my word for it that this number is not in any way made up.</p>
           <h3 name="edaf" id="edaf" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--p">The upshot</h3>
           <p name="b645" id="b645" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">There is no point in trying to work out if an email address is ‘valid’. A user is far more likely to enter a <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">wrong and valid</strong> email address than they are to enter an invalid one.</p>
           <p name="499e" id="499e" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Therefore, you are better off spending your time doing literally <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">any other thing</em> than trying to validate email addresses.</p>
           <h3 name="0190" id="0190" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--p">The 100% correct&nbsp;way</h3>
           <p name="8903" id="8903" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">Send your users an activation email<strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">.</strong> (That’s a bold full-stop for effect.)</p>
           <p name="9f4a" id="9f4a" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p graf--trailing">I have published a follow up to this post that looks at how to help prevent your users from entering a wrong email address in the first place. With real life code! Go. Read. <a href="https://medium.com/@david.gilbertson/how-to-reduce-incorrect-email-addresses-df3b70cb15a9#.3y39aii0e" data-href="https://medium.com/@david.gilbertson/how-to-reduce-incorrect-email-addresses-df3b70cb15a9#.3y39aii0e" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">https://medium.com/@david.gilbertson/how-to-reduce-incorrect-email-addresses-df3b70cb15a9#.3y39aii0e</a></p>
          </div>
         </div>
        </section>
